Dear Mr. Placencia: 
In general accordance with the project contract documents, we performed wave 
equation analyses to evaluate whether the concrete piles may be driven to the specified 
pile tip elevations with the proposed equipments for the above project. The wave equation 
analyses were conducted based on the information provided by your office, the subsurface 
conditions contained in the referenced report, and project plans and specifications. 
PROJECT CONSIDERATIONS 
The project involves construction of a new two-story waterfront facility at Drydock 2, 
supporting nuclear ship maintenance and repair operations at the Pearl Harbor Naval 
Shipyard and Intermediate Maintenance Facility (PHNSY & IMF).  
Based on review of the plans and specifications, we understand that the new P-270 
building will be supported on 24-inch octagonal precast, prestressed concrete piles, 
designed for an allowable compressive capacity of 100 tons with various tip elevations 
from -55 to -70 feet Mean Sea Level (MSL). Each pile location is required to be predrilled 
to elevations ranging between -35 and -40 feet MSL. 
A test pile program is required by the contract documents, consisting of driving and 
testing nine 24-inch octagonal concrete piles. To examine pile drivability for proposed 
Healy Tibbitts Builders, Inc. 
Page 2 
W.O. 7023-00 
June 25, 2014 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California 
hammers, a wave equation analysis is required for each test pile location where different 
subsurface conditions exist. The pile foundation layout is divided into six (6) groups with 
various predrill tip and pile tip elevations as presented on the Pile Location Plan, Sheet 
S-100 of the plans, and also summarized in the table below. 
All test piles are required to be cast an additional 10 feet longer than the design 
length measuring from cut-off to tip elevations. We assume the cut-off elevation to be 
+5 feet MSL.

Subsurface conditions contained in the referenced report are reflected in the wave 
equation analyses, to account for the various soil/rock conditions encountered in the 
borings. 
Hammer and Driving System 
We understand that a Delmag D30-23 single acting diesel hammer and/or Junttan 
HHS-9A hydraulic impact hammer is proposed for the pile driving operations. Based on the 
pile driving equipment data forms provided, the Delmag D30-23 hammer has a ram weight of 
6,600 pounds and a maximum stroke of 10.02 feet for a maximum rated energy of 66,100 
foot-pounds at the maximum pump setting. The Junttan HHS-9A hammer has a ram weight 
of 19,800 pounds for a maximum rated energy of 66,000 foot-pounds at a maximum stroke of 
3.3 feet. 
A pile cushion consisting of at least 9 inches of plywood cushion block is proposed 
for the pile driving operations. The plywood cushion blocks generally have cross section 
areas of approximately 568 square inches for the 24-inch octagonal concrete piles. 
Schematic details of the driving system are presented on the Pile and Driving Equipment 
Data Forms in the Appendix (Pages 1 and 2). 
Healy Tibbitts Builders, Inc.

Pile Details 
As mentioned previously, the specified concrete piles consist of 24-inch octagonal 
precast, prestressed concrete piles. The estimated design lengths range from 60 to 
75 feet, as shown in the above table. The test piles are required to be cast 10 feet longer 
than the estimated design length. 
We understand that the piles will be cast from concrete with a minimum 28-day 
unconfined compressive strength of 6,000 pounds per square inch (psi). We also 
understand that the maximum allowable compression and tensile stresses are specified to 
be 1,015 and 4,060 pounds per square inch (psi). 
WAVE EQUATION ANALYSES 
The wave equation analyses were performed using the computer program, 
GRLWEAP (Wave Equation Analysis of Pile Foundations), which is an extension of the 
WEAP87 program developed under the sponsorship of the Federal Highway 
Administration.  
Wave equation analyses were performed for ten cases based on the pile driving 
system proposed, required predrilling and pile driving tip elevations, and variation of 
subsurface conditions encountered in the borings, as summarized in the following table, 
for 24-inch concrete test piles at the specified locations.

Complete printouts of the wave equation analyses results for the ten analyzed 
cases are provided in the Appendix (Pages 1.1 through 10.15). Graphs showing the 
ultimate pile capacity versus the driving resistance are provided on Plates 1.1 through 
1.10.  
Driving Stresses 
Graphs showing the computed maximum compression and tensile stresses during 
driving are provided on Plates 2.1 through 2.10 for the ten analyzed cases. Please note 
that the graphs were prepared based on kips per square inch (ksi), which is equivalent to 
1,000 psi. 
Based on our analyses, the compressive stresses during the pile driving for 24-inch 
octagonal concrete piles are less than the allowable compression stresses of 4,060 psi. 
The compression stresses developed during pile driving did not exceed the allowable 
compression stresses for the full range of driving resistance at Pump Settings 1 through 4 
for Delmag D30-23 diesel hammer, as well as at the strokes from 1 to 3.3 feet for Junttan 
HHS-9A hydraulic impact hammer. 
Healy Tibbitts Builders, Inc. Page 5
W.O. 7023-00
June 25, 2014
The tensile stresses developed during the pile driving estimated for 24-inch
octagonal concrete piles are also less than the allowable tensile stress of 1,015 psi for the
full range of driving resistance at Pump Settings 1 through 4 and at the strokes from 1 to
3.3 feet for Delmag D30-23 diesel hammer and Junttan HHS-9A hydraulic hammer,
respectively.
Based on the above results and the anticipated subsurface conditions, it is our
professional opinion that the proposed pile driving equipments (Delmag D30-23 diesel or
Junttan HHS-9A hydraulic hammers) are capable of installing the 24-inch octagonal
concrete piles to the specified tip elevations, achieving the specified design allowable
compressive capacity of 100 tons without over-stressing the concrete piles.
Care should be carried out during pile driving, such as when pile driving resistance
is low or within predrilled depth, to reduce the potential for pile damage and high pile
tensile stress. The pump setting of the diesel hammer or stroke of hydraulic hammer
should be carefully controlled to reduce the potential for pile damage and/or
over-stressing.
CLOSURE
We appreciate the opportunity to be of service to you on this project. If you have
questions or need additional information concerning this report, please contact our office.
Respectfully submitted,

                           GRLWEAP - Version 2010                                
                  WAVE EQUATION ANALYSIS OF PILE FOUNDATIONS                     
          written by GRL Engineers, Inc. (formerly Goble Rausche Likins          
         and Associates, Inc.) with cooperation from Pile Dynamics, Inc.         
                 Copyright (c) 1998-2010, Pile Dynamics, Inc.                    
                   ABOUT THE WAVE EQUATION ANALYSIS RESULTS                      
The GRLWEAP program simulates the behavior of a preformed pile driven by         
either an impact hammer or a vibratory hammer.  The program is based on          
mathematical models, which describe motion and forces of hammer, driving         
system, pile and soil under the hammer action.  Under certain conditions,        
the models only crudely approximate, often complex, dynamic situations.          
A wave equation analysis generally relies on input data, which represents        
normal situations.  In particular, the hammer data file supplied with the        
program assumes that the hammer is in good working order.  All of the input      
data selected by the user may be the best available information at the time      
when the analysis is performed.  However, input data and therefore results       
may significantly differ from actual field conditions.                           
Therefore, the program authors recommend prudent use of the GRLWEAP results.     
Soil response and hammer performance should be verified by static and/or         
dynamic testing and measurements.  Estimates of bending or other local           
non-axial stresses and prestress effects must also be accounted for by the       
user.                                                                            
The calculated capacity - blow count relationship, i.e. the bearing graph,       
should be used in conjunction with observed blow counts for the capacity         
assessment of a driven pile.  Soil setup occurring after pile installation       
may produce bearing capacity values that differ substantially from those         
expected from a wave equation analysis due to soil setup or relaxation.  This    
is particularly true for pile driven with vibratory hammers.  The GRLWEAP user   
must estimate such effects and should also use proper care when applying blow    
counts from restrike because of the variability of hammer energy, soil           
resistance and blow count during early restriking.                               
Finally, the GRLWEAP capacities are ultimate values.  They MUST be reduced by    
means of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load.      
The selection of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the           
construction control, the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties      
in the loads, the importance of building and other factors.

                           GRLWEAP - Version 2010                                
                  WAVE EQUATION ANALYSIS OF PILE FOUNDATIONS                     
          written by GRL Engineers, Inc. (formerly Goble Rausche Likins          
         and Associates, Inc.) with cooperation from Pile Dynamics, Inc.         
                 Copyright (c) 1998-2010, Pile Dynamics, Inc.                    
                   ABOUT THE WAVE EQUATION ANALYSIS RESULTS                      
The GRLWEAP program simulates the behavior of a preformed pile driven by         
either an impact hammer or a vibratory hammer.  The program is based on          
mathematical models, which describe motion and forces of hammer, driving         
system, pile and soil under the hammer action.  Under certain conditions,        
the models only crudely approximate, often complex, dynamic situations.          
A wave equation analysis generally relies on input data, which represents        
normal situations.  In particular, the hammer data file supplied with the        
program assumes that the hammer is in good working order.  All of the input      
data selected by the user may be the best available information at the time      
when the analysis is performed.  However, input data and therefore results       
may significantly differ from actual field conditions.                           
Therefore, the program authors recommend prudent use of the GRLWEAP results.     
Soil response and hammer performance should be verified by static and/or         
dynamic testing and measurements.  Estimates of bending or other local           
non-axial stresses and prestress effects must also be accounted for by the       
user.                                                                            
The calculated capacity - blow count relationship, i.e. the bearing graph,       
should be used in conjunction with observed blow counts for the capacity         
assessment of a driven pile.  Soil setup occurring after pile installation       
may produce bearing capacity values that differ substantially from those         
expected from a wave equation analysis due to soil setup or relaxation.  This    
is particularly true for pile driven with vibratory hammers.  The GRLWEAP user   
must estimate such effects and should also use proper care when applying blow    
counts from restrike because of the variability of hammer energy, soil           
resistance and blow count during early restriking.                               
Finally, the GRLWEAP capacities are ultimate values.  They MUST be reduced by    
means of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load.      
The selection of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the           
construction control, the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties      
in the loads, the importance of building and other factors.

                  WAVE EQUATION ANALYSIS OF PILE FOUNDATIONS                     
          written by GRL Engineers, Inc. (formerly Goble Rausche Likins          
         and Associates, Inc.) with cooperation from Pile Dynamics, Inc.         
                 Copyright (c) 1998-2010, Pile Dynamics, Inc.                    
                   ABOUT THE WAVE EQUATION ANALYSIS RESULTS                      
The GRLWEAP program simulates the behavior of a preformed pile driven by         
either an impact hammer or a vibratory hammer.  The program is based on          
mathematical models, which describe motion and forces of hammer, driving         
system, pile and soil under the hammer action.  Under certain conditions,        
the models only crudely approximate, often complex, dynamic situations.          
A wave equation analysis generally relies on input data, which represents        
normal situations.  In particular, the hammer data file supplied with the        
program assumes that the hammer is in good working order.  All of the input      
data selected by the user may be the best available information at the time      
when the analysis is performed.  However, input data and therefore results       
may significantly differ from actual field conditions.                           
Therefore, the program authors recommend prudent use of the GRLWEAP results.     
Soil response and hammer performance should be verified by static and/or         
dynamic testing and measurements.  Estimates of bending or other local           
non-axial stresses and prestress effects must also be accounted for by the       
user.                                                                            
The calculated capacity - blow count relationship, i.e. the bearing graph,       
should be used in conjunction with observed blow counts for the capacity         
assessment of a driven pile.  Soil setup occurring after pile installation       
may produce bearing capacity values that differ substantially from those         
expected from a wave equation analysis due to soil setup or relaxation.  This    
is particularly true for pile driven with vibratory hammers.  The GRLWEAP user   
must estimate such effects and should also use proper care when applying blow    
counts from restrike because of the variability of hammer energy, soil           
resistance and blow count during early restriking.                               
Finally, the GRLWEAP capacities are ultimate values.  They MUST be reduced by    
means of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load.      
The selection of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the           
construction control, the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties      
in the loads, the importance of building and other factors.

                           GRLWEAP - Version 2010                                
                  WAVE EQUATION ANALYSIS OF PILE FOUNDATIONS                     
          written by GRL Engineers, Inc. (formerly Goble Rausche Likins          
         and Associates, Inc.) with cooperation from Pile Dynamics, Inc.         
                 Copyright (c) 1998-2010, Pile Dynamics, Inc.                    
                   ABOUT THE WAVE EQUATION ANALYSIS RESULTS                      
The GRLWEAP program simulates the behavior of a preformed pile driven by         
either an impact hammer or a vibratory hammer.  The program is based on          
mathematical models, which describe motion and forces of hammer, driving         
system, pile and soil under the hammer action.  Under certain conditions,        
the models only crudely approximate, often complex, dynamic situations.          
A wave equation analysis generally relies on input data, which represents        
normal situations.  In particular, the hammer data file supplied with the        
program assumes that the hammer is in good working order.  All of the input      
data selected by the user may be the best available information at the time      
when the analysis is performed.  However, input data and therefore results       
may significantly differ from actual field conditions.                           
Therefore, the program authors recommend prudent use of the GRLWEAP results.     
Soil response and hammer performance should be verified by static and/or         
dynamic testing and measurements.  Estimates of bending or other local           
non-axial stresses and prestress effects must also be accounted for by the       
user.                                                                            
The calculated capacity - blow count relationship, i.e. the bearing graph,       
should be used in conjunction with observed blow counts for the capacity         
assessment of a driven pile.  Soil setup occurring after pile installation       
may produce bearing capacity values that differ substantially from those         
expected from a wave equation analysis due to soil setup or relaxation.  This    
is particularly true for pile driven with vibratory hammers.  The GRLWEAP user   
must estimate such effects and should also use proper care when applying blow    
counts from restrike because of the variability of hammer energy, soil           
resistance and blow count during early restriking.                               
Finally, the GRLWEAP capacities are ultimate values.  They MUST be reduced by    
means of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load.      
The selection of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the           
construction control, the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties      
in the loads, the importance of building and other factors.

                           GRLWEAP - Version 2010                                
                  WAVE EQUATION ANALYSIS OF PILE FOUNDATIONS                     
          written by GRL Engineers, Inc. (formerly Goble Rausche Likins          
         and Associates, Inc.) with cooperation from Pile Dynamics, Inc.         
                 Copyright (c) 1998-2010, Pile Dynamics, Inc.                    
                   ABOUT THE WAVE EQUATION ANALYSIS RESULTS                      
The GRLWEAP program simulates the behavior of a preformed pile driven by         
either an impact hammer or a vibratory hammer.  The program is based on          
mathematical models, which describe motion and forces of hammer, driving         
system, pile and soil under the hammer action.  Under certain conditions,        
the models only crudely approximate, often complex, dynamic situations.          
A wave equation analysis generally relies on input data, which represents        
normal situations.  In particular, the hammer data file supplied with the        
program assumes that the hammer is in good working order.  All of the input      
data selected by the user may be the best available information at the time      
when the analysis is performed.  However, input data and therefore results       
may significantly differ from actual field conditions.                           
Therefore, the program authors recommend prudent use of the GRLWEAP results.     
Soil response and hammer performance should be verified by static and/or         
dynamic testing and measurements.  Estimates of bending or other local           
non-axial stresses and prestress effects must also be accounted for by the       
user.                                                                            
The calculated capacity - blow count relationship, i.e. the bearing graph,       
should be used in conjunction with observed blow counts for the capacity         
assessment of a driven pile.  Soil setup occurring after pile installation       
may produce bearing capacity values that differ substantially from those         
expected from a wave equation analysis due to soil setup or relaxation.  This    
is particularly true for pile driven with vibratory hammers.  The GRLWEAP user   
must estimate such effects and should also use proper care when applying blow    
counts from restrike because of the variability of hammer energy, soil           
resistance and blow count during early restriking.                               
Finally, the GRLWEAP capacities are ultimate values.  They MUST be reduced by    
means of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load.      
The selection of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the           
construction control, the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties      
in the loads, the importance of building and other factors.

                           GRLWEAP - Version 2010                                
                  WAVE EQUATION ANALYSIS OF PILE FOUNDATIONS                     
          written by GRL Engineers, Inc. (formerly Goble Rausche Likins          
         and Associates, Inc.) with cooperation from Pile Dynamics, Inc.         
                 Copyright (c) 1998-2010, Pile Dynamics, Inc.                    
                   ABOUT THE WAVE EQUATION ANALYSIS RESULTS                      
The GRLWEAP program simulates the behavior of a preformed pile driven by         
either an impact hammer or a vibratory hammer.  The program is based on          
mathematical models, which describe motion and forces of hammer, driving         
system, pile and soil under the hammer action.  Under certain conditions,        
the models only crudely approximate, often complex, dynamic situations.          
A wave equation analysis generally relies on input data, which represents        
normal situations.  In particular, the hammer data file supplied with the        
program assumes that the hammer is in good working order.  All of the input      
data selected by the user may be the best available information at the time      
when the analysis is performed.  However, input data and therefore results       
may significantly differ from actual field conditions.                           
Therefore, the program authors recommend prudent use of the GRLWEAP results.     
Soil response and hammer performance should be verified by static and/or         
dynamic testing and measurements.  Estimates of bending or other local           
non-axial stresses and prestress effects must also be accounted for by the       
user.                                                                            
The calculated capacity - blow count relationship, i.e. the bearing graph,       
should be used in conjunction with observed blow counts for the capacity         
assessment of a driven pile.  Soil setup occurring after pile installation       
may produce bearing capacity values that differ substantially from those         
expected from a wave equation analysis due to soil setup or relaxation.  This    
is particularly true for pile driven with vibratory hammers.  The GRLWEAP user   
must estimate such effects and should also use proper care when applying blow    
counts from restrike because of the variability of hammer energy, soil           
resistance and blow count during early restriking.                               
Finally, the GRLWEAP capacities are ultimate values.  They MUST be reduced by    
means of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load.      
The selection of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the           
construction control, the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties      
in the loads, the importance of building and other factors.

                           GRLWEAP - Version 2010                                
                  WAVE EQUATION ANALYSIS OF PILE FOUNDATIONS                     
          written by GRL Engineers, Inc. (formerly Goble Rausche Likins          
         and Associates, Inc.) with cooperation from Pile Dynamics, Inc.         
                 Copyright (c) 1998-2010, Pile Dynamics, Inc.                    
                   ABOUT THE WAVE EQUATION ANALYSIS RESULTS                      
The GRLWEAP program simulates the behavior of a preformed pile driven by         
either an impact hammer or a vibratory hammer.  The program is based on          
mathematical models, which describe motion and forces of hammer, driving         
system, pile and soil under the hammer action.  Under certain conditions,        
the models only crudely approximate, often complex, dynamic situations.          
A wave equation analysis generally relies on input data, which represents        
normal situations.  In particular, the hammer data file supplied with the        
program assumes that the hammer is in good working order.  All of the input      
data selected by the user may be the best available information at the time      
when the analysis is performed.  However, input data and therefore results       
may significantly differ from actual field conditions.                           
Therefore, the program authors recommend prudent use of the GRLWEAP results.     
Soil response and hammer performance should be verified by static and/or         
dynamic testing and measurements.  Estimates of bending or other local           
non-axial stresses and prestress effects must also be accounted for by the       
user.                                                                            
The calculated capacity - blow count relationship, i.e. the bearing graph,       
should be used in conjunction with observed blow counts for the capacity         
assessment of a driven pile.  Soil setup occurring after pile installation       
may produce bearing capacity values that differ substantially from those         
expected from a wave equation analysis due to soil setup or relaxation.  This    
is particularly true for pile driven with vibratory hammers.  The GRLWEAP user   
must estimate such effects and should also use proper care when applying blow    
counts from restrike because of the variability of hammer energy, soil           
resistance and blow count during early restriking.                               
Finally, the GRLWEAP capacities are ultimate values.  They MUST be reduced by    
means of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load.      
The selection of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the           
construction control, the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties      
in the loads, the importance of building and other factors.

                           GRLWEAP - Version 2010                                
                  WAVE EQUATION ANALYSIS OF PILE FOUNDATIONS                     
          written by GRL Engineers, Inc. (formerly Goble Rausche Likins          
         and Associates, Inc.) with cooperation from Pile Dynamics, Inc.         
                 Copyright (c) 1998-2010, Pile Dynamics, Inc.                    
                   ABOUT THE WAVE EQUATION ANALYSIS RESULTS                      
The GRLWEAP program simulates the behavior of a preformed pile driven by         
either an impact hammer or a vibratory hammer.  The program is based on          
mathematical models, which describe motion and forces of hammer, driving         
system, pile and soil under the hammer action.  Under certain conditions,        
the models only crudely approximate, often complex, dynamic situations.          
A wave equation analysis generally relies on input data, which represents        
normal situations.  In particular, the hammer data file supplied with the        
program assumes that the hammer is in good working order.  All of the input      
data selected by the user may be the best available information at the time      
when the analysis is performed.  However, input data and therefore results       
may significantly differ from actual field conditions.                           
Therefore, the program authors recommend prudent use of the GRLWEAP results.     
Soil response and hammer performance should be verified by static and/or         
dynamic testing and measurements.  Estimates of bending or other local           
non-axial stresses and prestress effects must also be accounted for by the       
user.                                                                            
The calculated capacity - blow count relationship, i.e. the bearing graph,       
should be used in conjunction with observed blow counts for the capacity         
assessment of a driven pile.  Soil setup occurring after pile installation       
may produce bearing capacity values that differ substantially from those         
expected from a wave equation analysis due to soil setup or relaxation.  This    
is particularly true for pile driven with vibratory hammers.  The GRLWEAP user   
must estimate such effects and should also use proper care when applying blow    
counts from restrike because of the variability of hammer energy, soil           
resistance and blow count during early restriking.                               
Finally, the GRLWEAP capacities are ultimate values.  They MUST be reduced by    
means of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load.      
The selection of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the           
construction control, the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties      
in the loads, the importance of building and other factors.

                           GRLWEAP - Version 2010                                
                  WAVE EQUATION ANALYSIS OF PILE FOUNDATIONS                     
          written by GRL Engineers, Inc. (formerly Goble Rausche Likins          
         and Associates, Inc.) with cooperation from Pile Dynamics, Inc.         
                 Copyright (c) 1998-2010, Pile Dynamics, Inc.                    
                   ABOUT THE WAVE EQUATION ANALYSIS RESULTS                      
The GRLWEAP program simulates the behavior of a preformed pile driven by         
either an impact hammer or a vibratory hammer.  The program is based on          
mathematical models, which describe motion and forces of hammer, driving         
system, pile and soil under the hammer action.  Under certain conditions,        
the models only crudely approximate, often complex, dynamic situations.          
A wave equation analysis generally relies on input data, which represents        
normal situations.  In particular, the hammer data file supplied with the        
program assumes that the hammer is in good working order.  All of the input      
data selected by the user may be the best available information at the time      
when the analysis is performed.  However, input data and therefore results       
may significantly differ from actual field conditions.                           
Therefore, the program authors recommend prudent use of the GRLWEAP results.     
Soil response and hammer performance should be verified by static and/or         
dynamic testing and measurements.  Estimates of bending or other local           
non-axial stresses and prestress effects must also be accounted for by the       
user.                                                                            
The calculated capacity - blow count relationship, i.e. the bearing graph,       
should be used in conjunction with observed blow counts for the capacity         
assessment of a driven pile.  Soil setup occurring after pile installation       
may produce bearing capacity values that differ substantially from those         
expected from a wave equation analysis due to soil setup or relaxation.  This    
is particularly true for pile driven with vibratory hammers.  The GRLWEAP user   
must estimate such effects and should also use proper care when applying blow    
counts from restrike because of the variability of hammer energy, soil           
resistance and blow count during early restriking.                               
Finally, the GRLWEAP capacities are ultimate values.  They MUST be reduced by    
means of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load.      
The selection of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the           
construction control, the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties      
in the loads, the importance of building and other factors.

                           GRLWEAP - Version 2010                                
                  WAVE EQUATION ANALYSIS OF PILE FOUNDATIONS                     
          written by GRL Engineers, Inc. (formerly Goble Rausche Likins          
         and Associates, Inc.) with cooperation from Pile Dynamics, Inc.         
                 Copyright (c) 1998-2010, Pile Dynamics, Inc.                    
                   ABOUT THE WAVE EQUATION ANALYSIS RESULTS                      
The GRLWEAP program simulates the behavior of a preformed pile driven by         
either an impact hammer or a vibratory hammer.  The program is based on          
mathematical models, which describe motion and forces of hammer, driving         
system, pile and soil under the hammer action.  Under certain conditions,        
the models only crudely approximate, often complex, dynamic situations.          
A wave equation analysis generally relies on input data, which represents        
normal situations.  In particular, the hammer data file supplied with the        
program assumes that the hammer is in good working order.  All of the input      
data selected by the user may be the best available information at the time      
when the analysis is performed.  However, input data and therefore results       
may significantly differ from actual field conditions.                           
Therefore, the program authors recommend prudent use of the GRLWEAP results.     
Soil response and hammer performance should be verified by static and/or         
dynamic testing and measurements.  Estimates of bending or other local           
non-axial stresses and prestress effects must also be accounted for by the       
user.                                                                            
The calculated capacity - blow count relationship, i.e. the bearing graph,       
should be used in conjunction with observed blow counts for the capacity         
assessment of a driven pile.  Soil setup occurring after pile installation       
may produce bearing capacity values that differ substantially from those         
expected from a wave equation analysis due to soil setup or relaxation.  This    
is particularly true for pile driven with vibratory hammers.  The GRLWEAP user   
must estimate such effects and should also use proper care when applying blow    
counts from restrike because of the variability of hammer energy, soil           
resistance and blow count during early restriking.                               
Finally, the GRLWEAP capacities are ultimate values.  They MUST be reduced by    
means of an appropriate factor of safety to yield a design or working load.      
The selection of a factor of safety should consider the quality of the           
construction control, the variability of the site conditions, uncertainties      
in the loads, the importance of building and other factors.                      
W.O. 7023-00
